     <p>The <b>University of California, Davis</b> (also referred to as <b>UCD</b>, <b>UC Davis</b>, or <b>Davis</b>) is a <a href="/wiki/Public_university" title="Public university">public</a> teaching and <a href="/wiki/Research_university" title="Research university" class="mw-redirect">research university</a> located in <a href="/wiki/Davis,_California" title="Davis, California">Davis</a>, <a href="/wiki/California" title="California">California</a> just west of <a href="/wiki/Sacramento" title="Sacramento" class="mw-redirect">Sacramento</a>. The campus covers 7,309 acres (2,958&nbsp;ha), making it the largest within the 10 campus <a href="/wiki/University_of_California" title="University of California">University of California</a> system and the second largest in California (behind <a href="/wiki/California_Polytechnic_State_University" title="California Polytechnic State University">California Polytechnic State University</a>). UC Davis also has the third largest enrollment in the UC System after <a href="/wiki/UCLA" title="UCLA" class="mw-redirect">UCLA</a> and <a href="/wiki/UC_Berkeley" title="UC Berkeley" class="mw-redirect">UC Berkeley</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Campus_Facts_4-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Campus_Facts-4"><span>[</span>4<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>UC Davis is a <a href="/wiki/Public_Ivy" title="Public Ivy">Public Ivy</a> with highly-ranked programs in the agricultural and biological sciences. The programs in engineering, the social sciences, physical sciences, mathematics, and humanities and the arts are also prestigious. UC Davis is also one of 62 members in the <a href="/wiki/Association_of_American_Universities" title="Association of American Universities">Association of American Universities</a>.</p> 
     <p>The <a href="/wiki/The_Carnegie_Foundation_for_the_Advancement_of_Teaching" title="The Carnegie Foundation for the Advancement of Teaching" class="mw-redirect">Carnegie Foundation</a> classifies UC Davis as a comprehensive <a href="/wiki/Doctoral" title="Doctoral" class="mw-redirect">doctoral</a> <a href="/wiki/Research_university" title="Research university" class="mw-redirect">research university</a> with a medical program, and very high research activity.<sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6"><span>[</span>6<span>]</span></a></sup> UC Davis faculty includes 21 members of the <a href="/wiki/United_States_National_Academy_of_Sciences" title="United States National Academy of Sciences" class="mw-redirect">National Academy of Sciences</a>, 21 members of the <a href="/wiki/American_Academy_of_Arts_and_Sciences" title="American Academy of Arts and Sciences">American Academy of Arts and Sciences</a>, 17 members of the <a href="/wiki/American_Law_Institute" title="American Law Institute">American Law Institute</a>, 12 members of the <a href="/wiki/Institute_of_Medicine" title="Institute of Medicine">Institute of Medicine</a>, and 13 members of the <a href="/wiki/National_Academy_of_Engineering" title="National Academy of Engineering">National Academy of Engineering</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FacultyAwards_7-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FacultyAwards-7"><span>[</span>7<span>]</span></a></sup> Among other honors, university faculty, alumni, and researchers have won the <a href="/wiki/Nobel_Peace_Prize" title="Nobel Peace Prize">Nobel Peace Prize</a>, <a href="/wiki/Presidential_Medal_of_Freedom" title="Presidential Medal of Freedom">Presidential Medal of Freedom</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pulitzer_Prize" title="Pulitzer Prize">Pulitzer Prize</a>, <a href="/wiki/MacArthur_Fellowship" title="MacArthur Fellowship" class="mw-redirect">MacArthur Fellowship</a>, <a href="/wiki/National_Medal_of_Science" title="National Medal of Science">National Medal of Science</a>, and <a href="/wiki/PECASE" title="PECASE" class="mw-redirect">Presidential Early Career Award in Science and Engineering</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FacultyAwards_7-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FacultyAwards-7"><span>[</span>7<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8"><span>[</span>8<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>The <a href="/wiki/UC_Davis_Aggies" title="UC Davis Aggies">UC Davis Aggies</a> athletic teams compete in the <a href="/wiki/National_Collegiate_Athletic_Association" title="National Collegiate Athletic Association">NCAA</a> <a href="/wiki/Division_I_(NCAA)" title="Division I (NCAA)">Division I</a> level, primarily in the <a href="/wiki/Big_West_Conference" title="Big West Conference">Big West Conference</a> as well as the <a href="/wiki/Big_Sky_Conference" title="Big Sky Conference">Big Sky Conference</a> (Football only) and the <a href="/wiki/Mountain_Pacific_Sports_Federation" title="Mountain Pacific Sports Federation">Mountain Pacific Sports Federation</a>. In its first year of full Division I status, 11 UC Davis teams qualified for NCAA post-season competition.</p>

     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_California,_Davis&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">edit</a>]</span></h2> 
     <div class="thumb tleft"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Creamery_and_Horticulture_buildings,_UC_Davis_(postcard).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ac/Creamery_and_Horticulture_buildings%2C_UC_Davis_%28postcard%29.jpg/220px-Creamery_and_Horticulture_buildings%2C_UC_Davis_%28postcard%29.jpg" width="220" height="136" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ac/Creamery_and_Horticulture_buildings%2C_UC_Davis_%28postcard%29.jpg/330px-Creamery_and_Horticulture_buildings%2C_UC_Davis_%28postcard%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ac/Creamery_and_Horticulture_buildings%2C_UC_Davis_%28postcard%29.jpg/440px-Creamery_and_Horticulture_buildings%2C_UC_Davis_%28postcard%29.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Creamery_and_Horticulture_buildings,_UC_Davis_(postcard).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf9/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> Early creamery and horticulture buildings, University Farm
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <div class="thumb tleft"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Ucdilo.jpeg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3e/Ucdilo.jpeg/220px-Ucdilo.jpeg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3e/Ucdilo.jpeg/330px-Ucdilo.jpeg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3e/Ucdilo.jpeg/440px-Ucdilo.jpeg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Ucdilo.jpeg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf9/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> The Silo Union, one of the original buildings
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>In 1905, Governor <a href="/wiki/George_Pardee" title="George Pardee">George Pardee</a> signed into law an act to establish a university farm school for the University of California (at the time, <a href="/wiki/University_of_California,_Berkeley" title="University of California, Berkeley">Berkeley</a> was the sole campus of the University). It would be more than a year before that commission selected a tiny town, then known as Davisville, as the site. What was to become the third UC Campus opened its doors to 40 degree students (all male) from UC Berkeley in January 1909 as the &quot;University Farm.&quot; (The farm had begun accepting non-degree farmers' short courses in October 1908; there were initially around 115 such attendees.) The establishment of the Farm was largely the result of the vision and perseverance of <a href="/wiki/Peter_J._Shields" title="Peter J. Shields">Peter J. Shields</a>, secretary of the State Agricultural Society, and the Peter J. Shields Library at UC Davis was named in his honor. Shields began to champion the cause of a University Farm to teach <a href="/wiki/Agriculture" title="Agriculture">agriculture</a> in a more applied fashion after hearing about California students who chose to go to out-of-state universities due to the lack of such programs in the University of California at that time. He later stated:</p> 
     <blockquote> 
      <p>There was a College of Agriculture at Berkeley in connection with the University of California, but it was purely academic. It was largely confined to the study of <a href="/wiki/Botany" title="Botany">botany</a> and chemistry; it had no farm and little prestige; it was apt to be thought of as a snap curriculum, attracting students who wanted to go to college but wanted to avoid its more difficult work.</p> 
     </blockquote> 
     <p>After two failed bills, a law authorizing the creation of a University Farm was passed on March 18, 1905, and <a href="/wiki/Yolo_County,_California" title="Yolo County, California">Yolo County</a>, home to some of California's prime farmland, was chosen as the site. The Farm accepted its first female students in 1914 from Berkeley. Renamed in 1922 the <i>Northern Branch of the College of Agriculture</i>, it continued growing at a breakneck pace: in 1916 the Farm's 314 students occupied the original 778 acres (315&nbsp;ha) campus, but by 1951 it had already expanded to a size of 3,000 acres (1,200&nbsp;ha). In 1959, the campus was declared by the <a href="/wiki/Regents_of_the_University_of_California" title="Regents of the University of California">Regents of the University of California</a> as the seventh general campus in the <a href="/wiki/University_of_California" title="University of California">University of California</a> system.</p> 
     <p>While UC Davis' agricultural heritage remains strong, the campus has expanded over the past century to include graduate and professional programs in <a href="/wiki/UC_Davis_School_of_Medicine" title="UC Davis School of Medicine">medicine</a> (which includes the <a href="/wiki/UC_Davis_Medical_Center" title="UC Davis Medical Center">UC Davis Medical Center</a>), <a href="/wiki/UC_Davis_School_of_Law" title="UC Davis School of Law">law</a>, <a href="/wiki/UC_Davis_School_of_Veterinary_Medicine" title="UC Davis School of Veterinary Medicine">veterinary medicine</a>, <a href="/wiki/UC_Davis_School_of_Education" title="UC Davis School of Education">education</a>, <a href="/wiki/Betty_Irene_Moore_School_of_Nursing" title="Betty Irene Moore School of Nursing">nursing</a>, and <a href="/wiki/UC_Davis_Graduate_School_of_Management" title="UC Davis Graduate School of Management">business management</a>, in addition to 90 research programs offered by <a href="/wiki/UC_Davis_Graduate_Studies" title="UC Davis Graduate Studies" class="mw-redirect">UC Davis Graduate Studies</a>. UC Davis' School of Veterinary Medicine is the largest in the United States and is ranked second in the nation.<sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9"><span>[</span>9<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="2011_pepper_spray_incident">2011 pepper spray incident</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_California,_Davis&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: 2011 pepper spray incident">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <div class="rellink relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article: 
      <a href="/wiki/UC_Davis_pepper-spray_incident" title="UC Davis pepper-spray incident">UC Davis pepper-spray incident</a>
     </div> 
     <p>During a November 18, 2011 <a href="/wiki/Occupy_UC_Davis" title="Occupy UC Davis" class="mw-redirect">protest</a> against tuition hikes, campus police Lieutenant John Pike used pepper spray on seated students. The incident drew international attention and led to further demonstrations, a formal investigation, and Pike's departure in July 2012.<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10"><span>[</span>10<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11"><span>[</span>11<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12"><span>[</span>12<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Campus">Campus</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_California,_Davis&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Campus">edit</a>]</span></h2> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:MrakHall_Arboretum.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/7/74/MrakHall_Arboretum.jpg/220px-MrakHall_Arboretum.jpg" width="220" height="289" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/7/74/MrakHall_Arboretum.jpg/330px-MrakHall_Arboretum.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/7/74/MrakHall_Arboretum.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:MrakHall_Arboretum.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf9/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> A view of Mrak Hall from the 
        <a href="/wiki/University_of_California,_Davis_Arboretum" title="University of California, Davis Arboretum">arboretum</a>
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:UC_Davis_Mondavi_Center.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ab/UC_Davis_Mondavi_Center.jpg/220px-UC_Davis_Mondavi_Center.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ab/UC_Davis_Mondavi_Center.jpg/330px-UC_Davis_Mondavi_Center.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ab/UC_Davis_Mondavi_Center.jpg/440px-UC_Davis_Mondavi_Center.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:UC_Davis_Mondavi_Center.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf9/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> 
        <a href="/wiki/Mondavi_Center" title="Mondavi Center">Mondavi Center</a>
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Size_and_location">Size and location</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_California,_Davis&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Size and location">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <p>The University of California, Davis campus is the largest campus in the UC system by land area, spanning 7,309 acres (2,957.8&nbsp;ha) across two counties: <a href="/wiki/Yolo_County" title="Yolo County" class="mw-redirect">Yolo</a> and <a href="/wiki/Solano_County" title="Solano County" class="mw-redirect">Solano</a>. Though named after the City of Davis, the campus is technically located adjacent to the City of Davis in an unincorporated part of Yolo and Solano counties. The main campus is located 15 miles (24.1&nbsp;km) west of <a href="/wiki/Sacramento,_California" title="Sacramento, California">Sacramento</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Sacramento_Valley" title="Sacramento Valley">Sacramento Valley</a>, part of California's <a href="/wiki/Central_Valley_(California)" title="Central Valley (California)">Central Valley</a>, and is adjacent to <a href="/wiki/Interstate_80" title="Interstate 80">Interstate Highway 80</a>. The Davis campus is the only school within the UC system with an <a href="/wiki/University_Airport" title="University Airport">airport</a>, just west of main campus, and is one of two UC schools with its own <a href="/wiki/University_of_California,_Davis_Fire_Department" title="University of California, Davis Fire Department" class="mw-redirect">fire department</a>; the other being <a href="/wiki/University_of_California,_Santa_Cruz" title="University of California, Santa Cruz">UCSC</a>. The campus is also conveniently located approximately an hour away from both San Francisco and the Napa Valley and two hours from Lake Tahoe. It is also one of only three schools in the University of California system, the others being <a href="/wiki/UC_Berkeley" title="UC Berkeley" class="mw-redirect">UC Berkeley</a> and <a href="/wiki/UC_Irvine" title="UC Irvine" class="mw-redirect">UC Irvine</a>, with a <a href="/wiki/Nuclear_physics" title="Nuclear physics">nuclear</a> lab.</p> 
     <p>The city of <a href="/wiki/Davis,_CA" title="Davis, CA" class="mw-redirect">Davis</a> is a <a href="/wiki/College_town" title="College town">college town</a>, with the ratio of students to long term residents estimated at 1:4. Also contributing to the college-town environment is the close proximity of downtown Davis to the campus' main quad?a matter of a few blocks, and 5-10 minute walk or bike ride. Davis' 15 minute distance from Sacramento provides it with both the isolation critical to fostering a college-town environment while also providing a lively and large metropolitan area nearby. Though the campus itself is vast, the entire community of Davis is relatively small and is easily traversable on bike utilizing Davis' extensive bicycle trails.</p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Campus_Core.2FQuad">Campus Core/Quad</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_California,_Davis&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Campus Core/Quad">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <p>Towards the northeast end of campus is the Quad, a large rectangular field, which was the historic geographic center of campus. Earlier in the campus' history, the few campus buildings surrounded the four sides of the Quad. Today, though the campus has grown significantly and the geographic center of campus has shifted, the Quad remains the center of campus life, anchored to the north by the Memorial Union (student union), to the south by Shields Library and to the West and Southeast by Wellman and Olson Halls respectively.</p> 
     <p>The Memorial Union Complex houses Freeborn Hall and the Memorial Union, which houses various establishments such as the UC Davis Bookstore, ASUCD Coffee House (Coho), ASUCD student government offices, Post Office, the MU Games Area (video games and bowling alley), KDVS student radio station, study lounges, Campus Copies, Picnic Day Office, the Center for Student Involvement Office, and AggieTV Student Television.</p> 
     <p>The northeast side of campus holds more of the core buildings that were built earlier in UC Davis's history, such as Wellman Hall, Shields Library, <a href="/wiki/Emil_M._Mrak" title="Emil M. Mrak">Mrak Hall</a>, and Hutchison Hall, as well as the North Entry Parking Structure. Also notable in this northeastern corner is the labyrinthine Social Sciences and Humanities building designed by <a href="/wiki/Antoine_Predock" title="Antoine Predock">Antoine Predock</a>, known to students as the &quot;<a href="/wiki/Death_Star" title="Death Star">Death Star</a>&quot; for its angular, metallic design.</p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="South_Main_Campus_.26_South_Campus">South Main Campus &amp; South Campus</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_California,_Davis&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: South Main Campus &amp; South Campus">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <p>The majority of Equestrian Center, and Animal Sciences buildings are located near the Arboretum Waterway, away from the core campus; the West Entry Parking Complex, the Silo Union, and the newly constructed Science Lecture Hall and the Science Laboratory Building are located nearer to the Tercero residence halls and the core of campus. The <a href="/wiki/Mondavi_Center" title="Mondavi Center">Mondavi Center</a>, home of the University Symphony Orchestra and other cultural events, is also located near the Tercero complex.</p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="West_Campus">West Campus</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_California,_Davis&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: West Campus">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <p>For most of UC Davis' history, West Campus has served primarily as agricultural research land. Recently, portions were developed through a $300 million public-private partnership to form the largest zero net energy community in the United States, known as UC Davis West Village.<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13"><span>[</span>13<span>]</span></a></sup> West Village will provide housing for 3,000 students, faculty and staff and will help the university recruit and retain top faculty. The project will include 662 apartments, 343 single-family homes, 42,500 square feet of commercial space, a recreation center and study facilities. West Village will also host the first community college on a UC campus.</p> 
     <p>The classes held in this area mainly involve plant sciences. Students in the classes maintain gardens as part of the PLS 5 lab.</p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Arboretum">Arboretum</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_California,_Davis&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Arboretum">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <p>To the south side of the campus core is the 100 acre <a href="/wiki/University_of_California,_Davis_Arboretum" title="University of California, Davis Arboretum">UC Davis Arboretum</a>, which includes 3.5 miles of paved paths, 4,000 tree specimens, Putah Creek and Lake Spafford.</p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Artwork">Artwork</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_California,_Davis&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Artwork">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <p>There are five public art statues found around campus, collectively called The Egghead Series, sculpted by former art professor <a href="/wiki/Robert_Arneson" title="Robert Arneson">Robert Arneson</a> who taught at Davis from 1962-1991 before his death in 1992. Additional pieces of Arneson's work are part of the Fine Arts Collection maintained by the Richard L. Nelson Gallery located in the Art Building.</p> 
     <p>&quot;Bookhead&quot; is located at the Shields Library plaza, &quot;Yin &amp; Yang&quot; is located at the Fine Arts Complex,&quot;See No Evil/Hear No Evil&quot; is at the east lawn of King Hall (the main building for UC Davis' School of Law), &quot;Eye on Mrak (FatalLaff)&quot; is outside Mrak Hall (housing the registrar office and other administrative offices), and &quot;Stargazer&quot; is located between North Hall and Young Hall. The &quot;Yin &amp; Yang&quot; egg heads have been recast and duplicated for installation near the Port of San Francisco Ferry Building in San Francisco.<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14"><span>[</span>14<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Student_housing">Student housing</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_California,_Davis&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Student housing">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <p>The northwest end of campus holds the majority of the Segundo undergraduate housing complex and various alternative non-undergraduate housing such as Orchard Park, Russell Park, and The Colleges at LaRue Apartments. The Activities and Recreation Center, or the ARC, is also located near the Segundo complex. Adjacent to the northwest corner of campus is the Cuarto undergraduate housing complex, which has one dining common.</p> 
     <p>The Tercero undergraduate housing complex is located near the true geographic center of the UC Davis campus, to the north of the Arboretum Waterway, which stretches longitudinally through almost the entirety of the south end of campus. The <a href="/wiki/University_of_California,_Davis,_Arboretum" title="University of California, Davis, Arboretum" class="mw-redirect">Davis Arboretum</a> is a public <a href="/wiki/Botanic_garden" title="Botanic garden" class="mw-redirect">botanic garden</a> with over 4,000 kinds of trees and plants, including many <a href="/wiki/California_native_plants" title="California native plants" class="mw-redirect">California native plants</a>, that stretches for over 100 acres (40&nbsp;ha) along The Waterway.</p> 
     <p>The Cuarto undergraduate (freshmen and transfer students) housing complex is located just one block off-campus, across Russell Boulevard. Unlike the other undergraduate housing complexes, Cuarto is located within city limits qualifying its residents to vote in city elections (other on-campus students can only vote in county elections).</p> 
     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Student_demographics">Student demographics</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_California,_Davis&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Student demographics">edit</a>]</span></h2>

     <p>In 2010, the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Census_Bureau" title="United States Census Bureau">United States Census Bureau</a> made UC Davis its own separate <a href="/wiki/Census-designated_place" title="Census-designated place">census-designated place</a> for statistical purposes.<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16"><span>[</span>16<span>]</span></a></sup> Most of the campus lies outside the Davis city limit. However, mail to the campus is still addressed, &quot;Davis, CA&quot;.</p> 
     <p>The <a href="/wiki/2010_United_States_Census" title="2010 United States Census">2010 United States Census</a><sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17"><span>[</span>17<span>]</span></a></sup> reported that University of California Davis had a population of 5,786. The <a href="/wiki/Population_density" title="Population density">population density</a> was 3,966.8 people per square mile (1,531.6/km&sup2;). The racial makeup of University of California Davis was 2,443 (42.2%) <a href="/wiki/White_(U.S._Census)" title="White (U.S. Census)" class="mw-redirect">White</a>, 144 (2.5%) <a href="/wiki/African_American_(U.S._Census)" title="African American (U.S. Census)" class="mw-redirect">African American</a>, 22 (0.4%) <a href="/wiki/Native_American_(U.S._Census)" title="Native American (U.S. Census)" class="mw-redirect">Native American</a>, 2,443 (42.2%) <a href="/wiki/Asian_(U.S._Census)" title="Asian (U.S. Census)" class="mw-redirect">Asian</a>, 7 (0.1%) <a href="/wiki/Pacific_Islander_(U.S._Census)" title="Pacific Islander (U.S. Census)" class="mw-redirect">Pacific Islander</a>, 364 (6.3%) from <a href="/wiki/Race_(United_States_Census)" title="Race (United States Census)" class="mw-redirect">other races</a>, and 363 (6.3%) from two or more races. <a href="/wiki/Hispanic_(U.S._Census)" title="Hispanic (U.S. Census)" class="mw-redirect">Hispanic</a> or <a href="/wiki/Latino_(U.S._Census)" title="Latino (U.S. Census)" class="mw-redirect">Latino</a> of any race were 728 persons (12.6%).</p> 
     <p>The Census reported that 2,561 people (44.3% of the population) lived in households, 3,225 (55.7%) lived in non-institutionalized group quarters, and 0 (0%) were institutionalized.</p> 
     <p>There were 1,096 households, out of which 203 (18.5%) had children under the age of 18 living in them, 292 (26.6%) were <a href="/wiki/Marriage" title="Marriage">opposite-sex married couples</a> living together, 59 (5.4%) had a female householder with no husband present, 16 (1.5%) had a male householder with no wife present. There were 34 (3.1%) <a href="/wiki/POSSLQ" title="POSSLQ">unmarried opposite-sex partnerships</a>, and 5 (0.5%) <a href="/wiki/Same-sex_partnerships" title="Same-sex partnerships" class="mw-redirect">same-sex married couples or partnerships</a>. 245 households (22.4%) were made up of individuals and 1 (0.1%) had someone living alone who was 65 years of age or older. The average household size was 2.34. There were 367 <a href="/wiki/Family_(U.S._Census)" title="Family (U.S. Census)">families</a> (33.5% of all households); the average family size was 2.75.</p> 
     <p>The population was spread out with 310 people (5.4%) under the age of 18, 4,298 people (74.3%) aged 18 to 24, 1,124 people (19.4%) aged 25 to 44, 41 people (0.7%) aged 45 to 64, and 13 people (0.2%) who were 65 years of age or older. The median age was 19.6 years. For every 100 females there were 82.2 males. For every 100 females age 18 and over, there were 80.5 males.</p> 
     <p>There were 1,125 housing units at an average density of 771.3 per square mile (297.8/km&sup2;), of which 1 (0.1%) were owner-occupied, and 1,095 (99.9%) were occupied by renters. The homeowner vacancy rate was 0%; the rental vacancy rate was 0.6%. 1 people (0% of the population) lived in owner-occupied housing units and 2,560 people (44.2%) lived in rental housing units.</p> 
     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Organization_and_administration">Organization and administration</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_California,_Davis&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Organization and administration">edit</a>]</span></h2> 
     <p>The entire <a href="/wiki/University_of_California" title="University of California">University of California</a> system is governed by The Regents, a 26-member board, as established under Article IX, Section 9 of the <a href="/wiki/California_Constitution" title="California Constitution" class="mw-redirect">California Constitution</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18"><span>[</span>18<span>]</span></a></sup> The board appoints the University's principal officers including the system-wide president and UC Davis Chancellor.&quot;</p> 
     <p>The UC Davis Chancellor is the Chief Executive Officer of an institution with a $3 billion annual budget, a $678 million research enterprise, 5,300-acre (2,100&nbsp;ha) central campus, 32,000 students and 28,000 employees. The current and sixth chancellor is <a href="/wiki/Linda_Katehi" title="Linda Katehi" class="mw-redirect">Linda Katehi</a>. The Chancellor has overall responsibility for the leadership, management, and administration of the campus and reports &quot;as an equal&quot; to the President of the University of California system, a position currently held by Mark Yudof.<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19"><span>[</span>19<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>The Offices of the Chancellor and Provost is headed by the Executive Vice-Chancellor and Provost (EVCP). In their capacity as Executive Vice-Chancellor, the EVCP shares with the Chancellor in the overall leadership and management of campus administration and operations, whereas as Provost, the EVCP is UC Davis' chief academic officer.</p> 
     <p>The Senior Staff provides executive support to the Offices of the Chancellor and Provost. The Council of Deans and Vice-Chancellor consists of the heads of the university's major academic and administrative units.<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20"><span>[</span>20<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>Students are most likely to interact with or be directly affected by the Office of Student Affairs, which is run by the Vice Chancellor of Student Affairs, currently Fred Wood, and by a variety of associate and assistant vice-chancellors. This office oversees many campus units including: Admissions, Athletics, Campus Recreation, Campus Unions, Counseling and Psychological Services, Financial Aid, Student Housing and others.<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21"><span>[</span>21<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Academics">Academics</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_California,_Davis&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Academics">edit</a>]</span></h2> 
     <p>The <a href="/wiki/University_of_California" title="University of California">University of California</a> system was considered by Richard Moll to be among America's <a href="/wiki/Public_Ivy" title="Public Ivy">Public Ivy</a> universities.<sup id="cite_ref-PublicIvys_22-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PublicIvys-22"><span>[</span>22<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23"><span>[</span>23<span>]</span></a></sup> The university has 102 undergraduate majors and 87 graduate programs.<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24"><span>[</span>24<span>]</span></a></sup> It has a <a href="/wiki/UC_Davis_Department_of_Viticulture_and_Enology" title="UC Davis Department of Viticulture and Enology">Department of Viticulture and Enology</a> (concerning the scientific study of grape-growing and winemaking) that has been and continues to be responsible for significant advancements in winemaking utilized by many Californian wineries. The campus is noted for its top-rated Agricultural and Resource Economics programs <sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25"><span>[</span>25<span>]</span></a></sup> and the large Department of Animal Science through which students can study at the university's own on-campus <a href="/wiki/Dairy" title="Dairy">dairy</a>, meat-processing plant, <a href="/wiki/Equestrianism" title="Equestrianism">equestrian</a> facility, and experimental farm. Students of Environmental Horticulture and other botanical sciences have many acres of campus farmland and the <a href="/wiki/University_of_California,_Davis,_Arboretum" title="University of California, Davis, Arboretum" class="mw-redirect">University of California, Davis, Arboretum</a> at their disposal. The <a href="/wiki/Department_of_Applied_Science,_UC_Davis" title="Department of Applied Science, UC Davis">Department of Applied Science</a> was founded and formerly chaired by physicist <a href="/wiki/Edward_Teller" title="Edward Teller">Edward Teller</a>. The arts are also studied extensively on campus with subjects such as studio art, design, music, theater and dance. The Design Department at UC Davis is the only comprehensive academic design unit of the University of California system.<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26"><span>[</span>26<span>]</span></a></sup> There is also the <a href="/wiki/Mondavi_Center" title="Mondavi Center">Mondavi Center</a> for the Performing Arts which features artists from all over the globe.</p> 
     <p>UC Davis undergraduate majors are divided into four colleges:</p> 
     <ul> 
      <li><a href="/wiki/UC_Davis_College_of_Agricultural_and_Environmental_Sciences" title="UC Davis College of Agricultural and Environmental Sciences">UC Davis College of Agricultural and Environmental Sciences</a></li> 
      <li><a href="/wiki/UC_Davis_College_of_Biological_Sciences" title="UC Davis College of Biological Sciences">UC Davis College of Biological Sciences</a></li> 
      <li><a href="/wiki/UC_Davis_College_of_Engineering" title="UC Davis College of Engineering">UC Davis College of Engineering</a></li> 
      <li><a href="/wiki/UC_Davis_College_of_Letters_and_Science" title="UC Davis College of Letters and Science">UC Davis College of Letters and Science</a></li> 
     </ul> 
     <p>UC Davis has the following graduate and professional schools, the most in the entire UC system&nbsp;:</p> 
     <ul> 
      <li><a href="/wiki/UC_Davis_Graduate_Studies" title="UC Davis Graduate Studies" class="mw-redirect">UC Davis Graduate Studies</a></li> 
      <li><a href="/wiki/UC_Davis_Graduate_School_of_Management" title="UC Davis Graduate School of Management">Graduate School of Management</a></li> 
      <li><a href="/wiki/UC_Davis_School_of_Education" title="UC Davis School of Education">School of Education</a></li> 
      <li><a href="/wiki/UC_Davis_School_of_Law" title="UC Davis School of Law">School of Law</a></li> 
      <li><a href="/wiki/UC_Davis_School_of_Medicine" title="UC Davis School of Medicine">School of Medicine</a></li> 
      <li><a href="/wiki/UC_Davis_School_of_Veterinary_Medicine" title="UC Davis School of Veterinary Medicine">School of Veterinary Medicine</a></li> 
      <li><a href="/wiki/Betty_Irene_Moore_School_of_Nursing" title="Betty Irene Moore School of Nursing">School of Nursing</a>.</li> 
     </ul> 
     <p>The university is host to the Army Reserve Officer Training Corps (ROTC) program, with more than 120 cadets. With more than sixty years in existence, it currently commissions roughly 30 to 40 graduating seniors as second lieutenants every year.<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27"><span>[</span>27<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Rankings">Rankings</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_California,_Davis&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Rankings">edit</a>]</span></h3>

     <p>UC Davis is considered a <a href="/wiki/Public_Ivy" title="Public Ivy">Public Ivy</a>. In 2013, <i><a href="/wiki/U.S._News_and_World_Report" title="U.S. News and World Report" class="mw-redirect">U.S. News and World Report</a></i> ranked UC Davis as the 8th best public university in the United States, 38th nationally, and tied for 3rd best of the UC schools with <a href="/wiki/UCSD" title="UCSD" class="mw-redirect">UCSD</a>, following <a href="/wiki/UC_Berkeley" title="UC Berkeley" class="mw-redirect">UC Berkeley</a> and <a href="/wiki/UCLA" title="UCLA" class="mw-redirect">UCLA</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-USNews_35-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-USNews-35"><span>[</span>35<span>]</span></a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/Washington_Monthly" title="Washington Monthly">Washington Monthly</a></i> ranked UC Davis 17th in its 2012 National College Ranking based on the school's contributions to society.<sup id="cite_ref-washingtonmonthly.com_36-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-washingtonmonthly.com-36"><span>[</span>36<span>]</span></a></sup> Also in 2012, <i><a href="/wiki/Forbes" title="Forbes">Forbes</a></i> ranked UC Davis as 128th overall in the nation, 15th among public institutions, 39th among national research universities, and 3rd in the University of California, after <a href="/wiki/UCLA" title="UCLA" class="mw-redirect">UCLA</a> and <a href="/wiki/UC_Berkeley" title="UC Berkeley" class="mw-redirect">UC Berkeley</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37"><span>[</span>37<span>]</span></a></sup> In 2013 <i><a href="/wiki/Kiplinger" title="Kiplinger">Kiplinger</a></i> ranked UC Davis 23rd out of the top 100 best-value public colleges and universities in the nation, and 6th in California.<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38"><span>[</span>38<span>]</span></a></sup> According to the 2011-2012 Top 50 Colleges and Universities in America published by <i>The Best Colleges</i>, UC Davis is ranked 27th nationally and 2nd among the UCs after <a href="/wiki/UC_Berkeley" title="UC Berkeley" class="mw-redirect">UC Berkeley</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39"><span>[</span>39<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>The university has several distinguished graduate programs ranked in the top 10 in their fields by the <a href="/wiki/United_States_National_Research_Council" title="United States National Research Council">United States National Research Council</a>; most notable are its programs in <a href="/wiki/Agricultural_economics" title="Agricultural economics">agricultural economics</a>, <a href="/wiki/Entomology" title="Entomology">entomology</a>, <a href="/wiki/Evolutionary_biology" title="Evolutionary biology">evolutionary biology</a>, <a href="/wiki/Plant_biology" title="Plant biology" class="mw-redirect">plant biology</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Ecology" title="Ecology">ecology</a>. Additionally, the NRC placed more than a third of UC Davis graduate programs in the top 25% of their respective fields.<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40"><span>[</span>40<span>]</span></a></sup> <i>U.S. News &amp; World Report</i> placed UC Davis 2nd nationally in Veterinary Medicine,3rd in Ecology / Evolutionary Biology, 7th in Biological / Agricultural Engineering, 11th in Environmental Engineering, 13th in Topology, 14th in U.S. Colonial History, 15th in International Economics, and 19th in American Politics in 2013.<sup id="cite_ref-USNews_35-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-USNews-35"><span>[</span>35<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>The <i><a href="/wiki/Academic_Ranking_of_World_Universities" title="Academic Ranking of World Universities">Academic Ranking of World Universities</a></i> placed UC Davis 33rd nationally and 47th globally for 2012. In 2011, <i><a href="/wiki/Times_Higher_Education_World_University_Rankings" title="Times Higher Education World University Rankings">Times Higher Education World University Rankings</a></i> ranked it 38th in the world, while the <i><a href="/wiki/QS_World_University_Rankings" title="QS World University Rankings">QS World University Rankings</a></i> ranked it 101st.</p> 
     <p><b>In 2012, <i><a href="/wiki/Sierra_Club" title="Sierra Club">Sierra Magazine</a></i> ranked UC Davis as 1st for &quot;Coolest School&quot; in America due to the school's sustainability and climate change efforts.<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41"><span>[</span>41<span>]</span></a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/Newsweek" title="Newsweek">Newsweek</a></i></b><i>s &quot;College Rankings 2011&quot; placed UC Davis 10th for &quot;Happiest Schools in America&quot; and 11th among the &quot;Greenest Schools&quot;in the United States.<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42"><span>[</span>42<span>]</span></a></sup> UC Davis was awarded an A- from the</i> 2010 College Sustainability Report Card<i>, which grades schools on their level of environmental sustainability across nine categories.<sup id="cite_ref-greenreportcard.org_43-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-greenreportcard.org-43"><span>[</span>43<span>]</span></a></sup> In 2011, UC Davis was also ranked 8th in</i> Sierra <i>magazine's national &quot;Cool Schools&quot; rankings which center on environmental goals and achievements.<sup id="cite_ref-sierracoolschool.27.27.27_44-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sierracoolschool.27.27.27-44"><span>[</span>44<span>]</span></a></sup></i></p> 
     <p>The city of Davis has been ranked as the 2d Best College Town in America<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45"><span>[</span>45<span>]</span></a></sup> and the Best College Downtown in California.<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46"><span>[</span>46<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Admissions">Admissions</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_California,_Davis&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Admissions">edit</a>]</span></h3>
