     </div> 
     <p>Admission to UC Davis is rated as &quot;most selective&quot; by <i><a href="/wiki/U.S._News_and_World_Report" title="U.S. News and World Report" class="mw-redirect">U.S. News and World Report</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52"><span>[</span>52<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>For Fall 2013, UC Davis received 55,895 freshmen applications; 21,998 were admitted (39.4%).<sup id="cite_ref-news.ucdavis.edu_47-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-news.ucdavis.edu-47"><span>[</span>47<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>UC Davis received 49,333 applications for admission to the Fall 2012 incoming freshman class; 22,521 were admitted (45.7%).<sup id="cite_ref-Profile2012_3-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Profile2012-3"><span>[</span>3<span>]</span></a></sup> The middle 50% of the 5,208 enrolled freshmen had average high school GPAs between 3.9-4.1, while the middle 50% range of SAT scores were 520-640 for critical reading, 570-690 for math, and 540-660 for writing.<sup id="cite_ref-Profile2012_3-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Profile2012-3"><span>[</span>3<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>For Fall 2012, 13,180 transfer applications were received; 7,673 were admitted (58.2%) and 2,888 enrolled.<sup id="cite_ref-Profile2012_3-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Profile2012-3"><span>[</span>3<span>]</span></a></sup> 93.2% of admitted transfer students were from California community colleges.<sup id="cite_ref-TransferAdmissions_53-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-TransferAdmissions-53"><span>[</span>53<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Library">Library</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_California,_Davis&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Library">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:UCDavis_PeterJShieldsLibrary.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/61/UCDavis_PeterJShieldsLibrary.jpg/220px-UCDavis_PeterJShieldsLibrary.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/61/UCDavis_PeterJShieldsLibrary.jpg/330px-UCDavis_PeterJShieldsLibrary.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/61/UCDavis_PeterJShieldsLibrary.jpg/440px-UCDavis_PeterJShieldsLibrary.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:UCDavis_PeterJShieldsLibrary.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf9/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> Inside of the Peter J. Shields Library
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>UC Davis' libraries include the <a href="/wiki/Peter_J._Shields_Library" title="Peter J. Shields Library" class="mw-redirect">Peter J. Shields Library</a>, the Physical Sciences &amp; Engineering Library, the Carlson Health Sciences Library, and the Medical Center Library in <a href="/wiki/Sacramento" title="Sacramento" class="mw-redirect">Sacramento</a>, contain more than 3.5 million volumes and offers a number of special collections and services. The Peter J. Shields Library has three different architectural styles due to various construction and extensions being added; it is the main library where students study on-campus, with a 24-hour reading room, open computer labs, and unique furniture.</p> 
     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Faculty_and_research">Faculty and research</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_California,_Davis&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Faculty and research">edit</a>]</span></h2> 
     <p>UC Davis is also one of 62 members in the prestigious <a href="/wiki/Association_of_American_Universities" title="Association of American Universities">Association of American Universities</a> (as of 1996). The Association of American Universities is an organization of leading research universities devoted to maintaining a strong system of academic research and education. It consists of sixty universities in the United States (both public and private) and two universities in Canada.</p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Research_expenditures">Research expenditures</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_California,_Davis&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Research expenditures">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <p>According to the <a href="/wiki/National_Science_Foundation" title="National Science Foundation">National Science Foundation</a>, UC Davis spent $456,653,000 on research and development in the fiscal year 2002-2003, ranking it 14th in the nation. Specifically, UC Davis's expenditures nationally ranked first in agricultural research ($25,683,000), seventh in biological research ($118,477,000), and 13th in the life sciences ($336,796,000). UC Davis reported $750 million in research expenditures in 2011-12.<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54"><span>[</span>54<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Faculty_honors">Faculty honors</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_California,_Davis&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Faculty honors">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <p>Its faculty includes 20 members of the <a href="/wiki/United_States_National_Academy_of_Sciences" title="United States National Academy of Sciences" class="mw-redirect">National Academy of Sciences</a>, 11 members of the <a href="/wiki/National_Academy_of_Engineering" title="National Academy of Engineering">National Academy of Engineering</a>, 21 members of the <a href="/wiki/American_Academy_of_Arts_and_Sciences" title="American Academy of Arts and Sciences">American Academy of Arts and Sciences</a>, 17 members of the <a href="/wiki/American_Law_Institute" title="American Law Institute">American Law Institute</a>, 2 <a href="/wiki/Pulitzer_Prize" title="Pulitzer Prize">Pulitzer Prize</a> winners, 2 <a href="/wiki/MacArthur_Fellowship" title="MacArthur Fellowship" class="mw-redirect">MacArthur Fellows</a> and one member of the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Society" title="Royal Society">Royal Society</a>.</p> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Bodega_Marine_Lab_3543.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c7/Bodega_Marine_Lab_3543.jpg/220px-Bodega_Marine_Lab_3543.jpg" width="220" height="112" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c7/Bodega_Marine_Lab_3543.jpg/330px-Bodega_Marine_Lab_3543.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c7/Bodega_Marine_Lab_3543.jpg/440px-Bodega_Marine_Lab_3543.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Bodega_Marine_Lab_3543.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf9/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> Bodega Marine Lab from the south, looking across Horseshoe Cove
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Research_centers_and_laboratories">Research centers and laboratories</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_California,_Davis&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Research centers and laboratories">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <p>The campus supports a number of research centers and laboratories including:</p> 
     <ul> 
      <li><a href="/wiki/AHMCT" title="AHMCT" class="mw-redirect">Advanced Highway Maintenance Construction Technology Research Laboratory</a></li> 
      <li>BGI at UC Davis Joint Genome Center (in planning process) <sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55"><span>[</span>55<span>]</span></a></sup></li> 
      <li>Bodega Bay Marine Laboratory</li> 
      <li>CalEPR Center</li> 
      <li>California National Primate Research Center</li> 
      <li>California Raptor Center</li> 
      <li><a href="/w/index.php?title=Center_for_Health_and_the_Environment&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Center for Health and the Environment (page does not exist)">Center for Health and the Environment</a></li> 
      <li><a href="/w/index.php?title=Center_for_the_Study_of_Human_Rights_in_the_Americas&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Center for the Study of Human Rights in the Americas (page does not exist)">Center for the Study of Human Rights in the Americas</a><sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56"><span>[</span>56<span>]</span></a></sup></li> 
      <li><a href="/w/index.php?title=Center_for_Visual_Sciences&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Center for Visual Sciences (page does not exist)">Center for Visual Sciences</a></li> 
      <li><a href="/w/index.php?title=Crocker_Nuclear_Laboratory&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Crocker Nuclear Laboratory (page does not exist)">Crocker Nuclear Laboratory</a></li> 
      <li>Davis Millimeter Wave Research Center (A joint effort of Agilent Technologies Inc. and UC Davis) (in planning process)</li> 
      <li><a href="/w/index.php?title=Information_Center_for_the_Environment&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Information Center for the Environment (page does not exist)">Information Center for the Environment</a></li> 
      <li><a href="/wiki/MIND_Institute" title="MIND Institute">MIND Institute</a></li> 
      <li>Tahoe Center for Environmental Sciences</li> 
      <li><a href="/w/index.php?title=UC_Center_Sacramento&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="UC Center Sacramento (page does not exist)">UC Center Sacramento</a><sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57"><span>[</span>57<span>]</span></a></sup></li> 
      <li><a href="/wiki/UCPRC" title="UCPRC" class="mw-redirect">University of California Pavement Research Center</a></li> 
      <li>Energy Efficiency Center (the very first university run Energy Efficiency Center in the Nation).</li> 
     </ul> 
     <p>The <a href="/w/index.php?title=Crocker_Nuclear_Laboratory&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Crocker Nuclear Laboratory (page does not exist)">Crocker Nuclear Laboratory</a> on campus has had a <a href="/wiki/Nuclear_accelerator" title="Nuclear accelerator" class="mw-redirect">nuclear accelerator</a> since 1966.<sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58"><span>[</span>58<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Crocker_at_40_59-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Crocker_at_40-59"><span>[</span>59<span>]</span></a></sup> The laboratory is used by scientists and engineers from private industry, universities and government to research topics including <a href="/wiki/Nuclear_physics" title="Nuclear physics">nuclear physics</a>, applied <a href="/wiki/Solid_state_physics" title="Solid state physics" class="mw-redirect">solid state physics</a>, <a href="/wiki/Radiation" title="Radiation">radiation</a> effects, and <a href="/wiki/Planetary_geology" title="Planetary geology">planetary geology</a> and <a href="/w/index.php?title=Cosmogenics&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Cosmogenics (page does not exist)">cosmogenics</a> <sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60"><span>[</span>60<span>]</span></a></sup> UC Davis is the only UC campus, besides Berkeley, that has a nuclear laboratory.</p> 
     <p>Agilent Technologies will also work with the university in establishing a Davis Millimeter Wave Research Center to conduct research on millimeter wave and THz systems.<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61"><span>[</span>61<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Student_life">Student life</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_California,_Davis&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Student life">edit</a>]</span></h2> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Ucdarc.jpeg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/46/Ucdarc.jpeg/220px-Ucdarc.jpeg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/46/Ucdarc.jpeg/330px-Ucdarc.jpeg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/46/Ucdarc.jpeg/440px-Ucdarc.jpeg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Ucdarc.jpeg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf9/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> The Activities and Recreation Center
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>The undergraduate student government of UC Davis is the Associated Students of UC Davis (ASUCD), and has an annual operating budget of 11.1 million dollars, making it one of the largest-funded student government in the United States.<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62"><span>[</span>62<span>]</span></a></sup> ASUCD includes an Executive, Legislative, and Judicial branch. Other than representing the student body on campus, the task of ASUCD is to lobby student interests to local and state government. Also under the purview of ASUCD are the student-run Coffee House is an ASUCD unit and <a href="/wiki/Unitrans" title="Unitrans">Unitrans</a>, the Davis public bus system. ASUCD employs thousands of students<sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63"><span>[</span>63<span>]</span></a></sup> annually across its many units.</p> 
     <div class="thumb tleft"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Ucdavis_aggies.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/c/cc/Ucdavis_aggies.png/220px-Ucdavis_aggies.png" width="220" height="229" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/c/cc/Ucdavis_aggies.png/330px-Ucdavis_aggies.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/c/cc/Ucdavis_aggies.png 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Ucdavis_aggies.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf9/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> UC Davis Athletics logo
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:UC_Davis_Marching_Band.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a0/UC_Davis_Marching_Band.jpg/220px-UC_Davis_Marching_Band.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a0/UC_Davis_Marching_Band.jpg/330px-UC_Davis_Marching_Band.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a0/UC_Davis_Marching_Band.jpg/440px-UC_Davis_Marching_Band.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:UC_Davis_Marching_Band.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf9/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> 
        <a href="/wiki/UC_Davis_California_Aggie_Marching_Band-uh!" title="UC Davis California Aggie Marching Band-uh!">UC Davis California Aggie Marching Band-uh!</a>
        <sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64"><span>[</span>64<span>]</span></a></sup>
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p><a href="/wiki/Picnic_Day_(UC_Davis)" title="Picnic Day (UC Davis)">Picnic Day</a>, UC Davis's annual Open House, is the largest student-run event in the United States. It attracts thousands of visitors each year with its many attractions. These include a parade, a magic show performed by the chemistry department, the Doxie Derby (<a href="/wiki/Dachshund" title="Dachshund">dachshund</a> races), film screenings, and a <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_the_Bands" title="Battle of the Bands" class="mw-redirect">Battle of the Bands</a> between the <a href="/wiki/UC_Davis_California_Aggie_Marching_Band" title="UC Davis California Aggie Marching Band" class="mw-redirect">Band</a> and other college bands including the <a href="/wiki/Cal_Band" title="Cal Band" class="mw-redirect">Cal Band</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Stanford_Band" title="Stanford Band">Stanford Band</a>, and the Humboldt State Marching Band.</p> 
     <p>Another highlight of UC Davis is its student-run <a href="/wiki/Freeform_(radio_format)" title="Freeform (radio format)">freeform</a> radio station, <a href="/wiki/KDVS" title="KDVS">KDVS</a>. The station began operations on February 1, 1964 from the laundry room of the all-male dormitory Beckett Hall. The station soon gained a reputation by airing interviews with <a href="/wiki/Angela_Davis" title="Angela Davis">Angela Davis</a> and a live call-in show with then <a href="/wiki/Governor_of_California" title="Governor of California">California Governor</a> <a href="/wiki/Ronald_Reagan" title="Ronald Reagan">Ronald Reagan</a> in 1969. The station can now be heard on 90.3 <a href="/wiki/FM_broadcasting" title="FM broadcasting">FM</a> and online at its website.<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65"><span>[</span>65<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>UC Davis has some 400 registered student organizations, ranging from political clubs to professional societies to language clubs. Student clubs are managed through the Student Programs and Activities Center (SPAC).<sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66"><span>[</span>66<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>The academic Graduate Students and management students are represented by the Graduate Student Association (GSA). The Law Students are represented by Law Students Association.</p> 
     <p>Students are also encouraged to wear Aggie Blue on game days to show their Aggie Pride. If spotted wearing Aggie Blue by the Aggie Pack, students may have UC Davis paraphernalia thrown at them as a reward.</p> 
     <p>Students also participate in intramural sports such as basketball, ultimate frisbee, soccer and many more. The ARC contains a basketball gym, work out room, rock climbing wall, and other studio rooms for group exercise.</p> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Tai_Kwon_Do_competition,_UCD.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3e/Tai_Kwon_Do_competition%2C_UCD.jpg/220px-Tai_Kwon_Do_competition%2C_UCD.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3e/Tai_Kwon_Do_competition%2C_UCD.jpg/330px-Tai_Kwon_Do_competition%2C_UCD.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3e/Tai_Kwon_Do_competition%2C_UCD.jpg/440px-Tai_Kwon_Do_competition%2C_UCD.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Tai_Kwon_Do_competition,_UCD.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf9/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> The UC Davis Tae Kwon Do club
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>One less-known student tradition occurs during the commencement ceremonies, where students toss tortillas into the air at the beginning of the ceremony. Tortillas are smuggled into the building under graduation gowns and released into the air after all the graduates have taken their seats.</p> 
     <p>Other student activities</p> 
     <ul> 
      <li><a href="/wiki/Unitrans" title="Unitrans">Unitrans</a>, the student run (and driven) bus system.</li> 
      <li>The Coffee House, also known as the CoHo, is a student run restaurant serving 7000 customers daily.</li> 
      <li>The Bike Barn, a bicycle shop that sells and rents bicycles and cycling equipment, also operating a repair shop.</li> 
      <li><a href="/wiki/KDVS" title="KDVS">KDVS</a>, student radio.<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67"><span>[</span>67<span>]</span></a></sup></li> 
      <li>The Entertainment Council,<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68"><span>[</span>68<span>]</span></a></sup> responsible for bringing famous musicians to campus and organizing student events.<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69"><span>[</span>69<span>]</span></a></sup></li> 
      <li>US Post Office, a completely student-run official United States Postal Service Contract Station.</li> 
     </ul> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Transportation">Transportation</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_California,_Davis&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Transportation">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Bicycles,_UC_Davis.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ca/Bicycles%2C_UC_Davis.jpg/220px-Bicycles%2C_UC_Davis.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ca/Bicycles%2C_UC_Davis.jpg/330px-Bicycles%2C_UC_Davis.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ca/Bicycles%2C_UC_Davis.jpg/440px-Bicycles%2C_UC_Davis.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Bicycles,_UC_Davis.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf9/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> Bicycles, UC Davis
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Double-decker_bus,_UC_Davis.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/41/Double-decker_bus%2C_UC_Davis.jpg/220px-Double-decker_bus%2C_UC_Davis.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/41/Double-decker_bus%2C_UC_Davis.jpg/330px-Double-decker_bus%2C_UC_Davis.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/41/Double-decker_bus%2C_UC_Davis.jpg/440px-Double-decker_bus%2C_UC_Davis.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Double-decker_bus,_UC_Davis.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf9/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> One of the 
        <a href="/wiki/Double_decker" title="Double decker">double deckers</a> in the city's student-run (and student-driven) bus system
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>Bicyclists are ubiquitous around campus as well as the city, and thus a lot of bike-only infrastructure exists, such as bike circles, large bike lanes, and traffic signals exclusively for bikes and the UC Davis cycling team has won several national championship titles.<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70"><span>[</span>70<span>]</span></a></sup> The campus police department also has some of its officers patrol on bicycles and take bicycling under the influence (&quot;BUI&quot;) and bicycling without a headlight at night very seriously. All bikes on the UC Davis campus must be registered with a California Bicycle license or they risk being sold at the on campus bike auction.</p> 
     <p>UC Davis is also well known for its bus service, <a href="/wiki/Unitrans" title="Unitrans">Unitrans</a>, and its trademark London <a href="/wiki/Double-decker_bus" title="Double-decker bus">double decker buses</a>. It has been in operation since 1968 and is believed to be the only general purpose (non-sightseeing) transit system in the U.S. to operate vintage double deck buses in daily service. The system is operated and managed entirely by students and offers fixed-route transportation throughout the city. There is also an inter-campus bus service<sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71"><span>[</span>71<span>]</span></a></sup> that ferries back and forth between UC Davis and <a href="/wiki/UC_Berkeley" title="UC Berkeley" class="mw-redirect">UC Berkeley</a> twice daily, from Monday to Friday.</p> 
     <p>The central campus is bounded by freeways on two sides (Highway 113 and <a href="/wiki/Interstate_80" title="Interstate 80">Interstate 80</a>). All other UC campuses are either somewhat distant from the closest freeway or are directly adjacent to only one freeway. Two freeway exits are entirely within UCD's boundaries. One, off Highway 113, is signed &quot;UC Davis / Hutchison Drive&quot; and the other, off Interstate 80, is signed exclusively as &quot;UC Davis.&quot;</p> 
     <p>Easy freeway access, coupled with increasing housing costs in the city of Davis, have led to increased numbers of students commuting via automobile. Some students choose to live in the neighboring communities of <a href="/wiki/Sacramento,_CA" title="Sacramento, CA" class="mw-redirect">Sacramento</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dixon,_CA" title="Dixon, CA" class="mw-redirect">Dixon</a> or <a href="/wiki/Woodland,_CA" title="Woodland, CA" class="mw-redirect">Woodland</a>, and use their own cars or the county-wide Yolobus to get to UC Davis.</p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="The_California_Aggie"><i>The California Aggie</i></span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_California,_Davis&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: The California Aggie">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <p>UC Davis also publishes a daily <a href="/wiki/Student_newspaper" title="Student newspaper">student newspaper</a>, <i><a href="/wiki/The_California_Aggie" title="The California Aggie">The California Aggie</a></i>. The <i>Aggie</i> was first published in 1915 as the <i>Weekly Agricola</i> after its approval by the Associated Student Executive Committee. At this point, UC Davis was considered the University Farm, an extension of <a href="/wiki/UC_Berkeley" title="UC Berkeley" class="mw-redirect">UC Berkeley</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-ucdavis.edu_72-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ucdavis.edu-72"><span>[</span>72<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>Initially, the <i>Weekly Agricola</i> was focused on both student news and farming-related topics. Novelist <a href="/wiki/Jack_London" title="Jack London">Jack London</a> was one of the first readers of the <i>Weekly Agricola</i>. In 1922, it was renamed to match the school's athletic name.<sup id="cite_ref-ucdavis.edu_72-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ucdavis.edu-72"><span>[</span>72<span>]</span></a></sup> Today, the <i>Aggie</i> has the largest print distribution in <a href="/wiki/Yolo_County" title="Yolo County" class="mw-redirect">Yolo County</a>, at around 12,000 copies distributed daily.</p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Greek_life">Greek life</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_California,_Davis&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Greek life">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Water_Tower,_UC_Davis(cropped).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/40/Water_Tower%2C_UC_Davis%28cropped%29.jpg/170px-Water_Tower%2C_UC_Davis%28cropped%29.jpg" width="170" height="273" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/40/Water_Tower%2C_UC_Davis%28cropped%29.jpg/255px-Water_Tower%2C_UC_Davis%28cropped%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/40/Water_Tower%2C_UC_Davis%28cropped%29.jpg/340px-Water_Tower%2C_UC_Davis%28cropped%29.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Water_Tower,_UC_Davis(cropped).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf9/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> UC Davis' iconic water tower
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>Social fraternities and sororities have been a part of the University of California at Davis since 1913. Approximately 8% of the university's undergraduate students are involved in the school's fraternities and sororities. One sorority, <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.sigmaaepi.com"></a><a href="/wiki/Sigma_Alpha_Epsilon_Pi" title="Sigma Alpha Epsilon Pi">Sigma Alpha Epsilon Pi</a>, was featured during the first season of the MTV reality show &quot;Sorority Life.&quot;</p> 
     <p>There are currently 16 fraternities that are a part of the Interfraternity Council (IFC) in Davis. The IFC representatives attend weekly meetings to guarantee that all UC Davis rules and regulations are followed. The meetings are also used to inform the fraternities about all upcoming activities throughout the week. The 16 fraternities are: <a href="/wiki/Alpha_Epsilon_Pi" title="Alpha Epsilon Pi">Alpha Epsilon Pi</a>, <a href="/wiki/Alpha_Gamma_Omega" title="Alpha Gamma Omega">Alpha Gamma Omega</a>, <a href="/wiki/Alpha_Sigma_Phi" title="Alpha Sigma Phi">Alpha Sigma Phi</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chi_Phi" title="Chi Phi">Chi Phi</a>, <a href="/wiki/Delta_Chi" title="Delta Chi">Delta Chi</a>, <a href="/wiki/Delta_Sigma_Phi" title="Delta Sigma Phi">Delta Sigma Phi</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lambda_Chi_Alpha" title="Lambda Chi Alpha">Lambda Chi Alpha</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pi_Kappa_Alpha" title="Pi Kappa Alpha">Pi Kappa Alpha</a>, <a href="/wiki/Phi_Kappa_Psi" title="Phi Kappa Psi">Phi Kappa Psi</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sigma_Alpha_Mu" title="Sigma Alpha Mu">Sigma Alpha Mu</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sigma_Chi" title="Sigma Chi">Sigma Chi</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sigma_Nu" title="Sigma Nu">Sigma Nu</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sigma_Phi_Epsilon" title="Sigma Phi Epsilon">Sigma Phi Epsilon</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tau_Kappa_Epsilon" title="Tau Kappa Epsilon">Tau Kappa Epsilon</a>, <a href="/wiki/Theta_Chi" title="Theta Chi">Theta Chi</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Theta_Xi" title="Theta Xi">Theta Xi</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73"><span>[</span>73<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>The Panehellenic Council is similar to the Interfraternity Council, but is the governing council for several sororities at UC Davis. They are responsible for organizing recruitment, and overseeing that all regulations are upheld. There are currently 8 sororities that are a part of the Panhellenic Council. The 8 sororities are: <a href="/wiki/Alpha_Chi_Omega" title="Alpha Chi Omega">Alpha Chi Omega</a>, <a href="/wiki/Alpha_Phi" title="Alpha Phi">Alpha Phi</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chi_Omega" title="Chi Omega">Chi Omega</a>, <a href="/wiki/Delta_Delta_Delta" title="Delta Delta Delta">Delta Delta Delta</a>, <a href="/wiki/Delta_Gamma" title="Delta Gamma">Delta Gamma</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kappa_Alpha_Theta" title="Kappa Alpha Theta">Kappa Alpha Theta</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kappa_Kappa_Gamma" title="Kappa Kappa Gamma">Kappa Kappa Gamma</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Pi_Beta_Phi" title="Pi Beta Phi">Pi Beta Phi</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74"><span>[</span>74<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>The Phi Chapter of <a href="/wiki/Alpha_Gamma_Rho" title="Alpha Gamma Rho">Alpha Gamma Rho</a> was locally established May 1 of 1923 at UC Davis making it the first continuously running national fraternity on campus. They started as the Kappa Tau Fraternity, which was the first Agricultural Fraternity on campus. Many campus buildings are named after alumni of Alpha Gamma Rho such as Emil Mrak (Mrak Hall, Registrar's office), Orville Thompson (Thompson Hall, Segundo student housing), and Dean De Carli (the De Carli room, 2nd floor MU), Mel Olson Scoreboard (<a href="/wiki/Aggie_Stadium_(UC_Davis)" title="Aggie Stadium (UC Davis)">Aggie Stadium</a>), and many more. The AGR Hall is an event space located inside the Buehler Alumni / Visitor's Center and is commonly rented out as a conference room or banquet hall. There are both national and local fraternities and sororities at UCD with diverse backgrounds and histories.<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75"><span>[</span>75<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Athletics">Athletics</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_California,_Davis&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Athletics">edit</a>]</span></h2> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Aggie_Stadium_(UC_Davis).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Aggie_Stadium_%28UC_Davis%29.jpg/220px-Aggie_Stadium_%28UC_Davis%29.jpg" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Aggie_Stadium_%28UC_Davis%29.jpg/330px-Aggie_Stadium_%28UC_Davis%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Aggie_Stadium_%28UC_Davis%29.jpg/440px-Aggie_Stadium_%28UC_Davis%29.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Aggie_Stadium_(UC_Davis).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf9/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> 
        <a href="/wiki/Aggie_Stadium_(UC_Davis)" title="Aggie Stadium (UC Davis)">Aggie Stadium</a>
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <div class="rellink relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article: 
      <a href="/wiki/UC_Davis_Aggies" title="UC Davis Aggies">UC Davis Aggies</a>
     </div> 
     <p>The <a href="/wiki/UC_Davis_Aggies" title="UC Davis Aggies">UC Davis Aggies</a> (or Ags) compete in <a href="/wiki/National_Collegiate_Athletic_Association" title="National Collegiate Athletic Association">NCAA</a> <a href="/wiki/Division_I_(NCAA)" title="Division I (NCAA)">Division I</a> sports in the <a href="/wiki/Big_West_Conference" title="Big West Conference">Big West Conference</a>. For <a href="/wiki/American_football" title="American football">football</a>, the Aggies compete in Division I <a href="/wiki/Division_I_Football_Championship_Subdivision" title="Division I Football Championship Subdivision" class="mw-redirect">FCS</a> (formerly known as Division I-AA), and are members of the <a href="/wiki/Big_Sky_Conference" title="Big Sky Conference">Big Sky Conference</a>, granting UC Davis the distinction of being one of only three UC campuses to field a football team (<a href="/wiki/University_of_California,_Berkeley" title="University of California, Berkeley">Cal</a> and <a href="/wiki/University_of_California,_Los_Angeles" title="University of California, Los Angeles">UCLA</a> being the other two). The Aggies are also members of the <a href="/wiki/Mountain_Pacific_Sports_Federation" title="Mountain Pacific Sports Federation">Mountain Pacific Sports Federation</a> in gymnastics and lacrosse, the <a href="/wiki/Western_Intercollegiate_Rowing_Association" title="Western Intercollegiate Rowing Association">Western Intercollegiate Rowing Association</a> and <a href="/wiki/Davis_Men%27s_Crew_Club" title="Davis Men's Crew Club">Davis Men's Crew Club</a> for <a href="/wiki/Rowing_(sport)" title="Rowing (sport)">rowing</a>.</p> 
     <p>The UC <a href="/wiki/Davis_Men%27s_Crew_Club" title="Davis Men's Crew Club">Davis Men's Crew Club</a> is one of the more successful clubs both on campus and in the West. In 2008 the JV boat won first in nationals at the ACRA Championships in Tennessee and in 2009 the Varsity boat got second place in nationals at the ACRA Championships. They consistently compete against teams such as Stanford, the University of Washington and UC Berkeley.</p> 
     <p>The Aggies finished first in <a href="/wiki/National_Collegiate_Athletic_Association" title="National Collegiate Athletic Association">NCAA</a> <a href="/wiki/Division_II_(NCAA)" title="Division II (NCAA)">Division II</a> six times in 2003 and won the <a href="/wiki/NACDA_Directors%27_Cup" title="NACDA Directors' Cup">NACDA Directors' Cup</a> 4 years in a row from 1999 to 2003. In 1998, the UC Davis men's basketball team won the NCAA <a href="/wiki/Division_II_(NCAA)" title="Division II (NCAA)">Division II</a> national championship despite being one of the few non-scholarship institutions in Division II at that time. They have also won NCAA Division II championships in Softball (2003), Men's Tennis (1992), and Women's Tennis (1990, 1993). These and other achievements motivated a decision (following a year of heavy discussion by campus administrators, faculty, staff, students, alumni and the local community) in 2003 for the athletics program to re-classify to Division I.<sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76"><span>[</span>76<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77"><span>[</span>77<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Aggies_at_Stanford_(half-time_show).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7c/Aggies_at_Stanford_%28half-time_show%29.jpg/220px-Aggies_at_Stanford_%28half-time_show%29.jpg" width="220" height="293" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7c/Aggies_at_Stanford_%28half-time_show%29.jpg/330px-Aggies_at_Stanford_%28half-time_show%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7c/Aggies_at_Stanford_%28half-time_show%29.jpg/440px-Aggies_at_Stanford_%28half-time_show%29.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Aggies_at_Stanford_(half-time_show).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf9/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> Aggies at Stanford (half-time show), September 17, 2005
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>The highlight of the recent 4-year transition to Division I occurred on September 17, 2005, when the Aggies defeated the heavily favored <a href="/wiki/Stanford_Cardinal" title="Stanford Cardinal">Stanford Cardinal</a> at <a href="/wiki/Stanford_Stadium" title="Stanford Stadium">Stanford Stadium</a> by a score of 20-17 on a TD pass with 8 seconds left in the game. The Aggies also pulled off an upset against Stanford in basketball just months later, beating the Cardinal 64-58 with a late rally at home on December 4, 2005. The win in these two major sports and the addition of the Aggies beating the Cardinal in soccer earlier in 2005 as well as a win in wrestling and two wins in baseball pulled the Aggies' win loss record with Stanford to 5-1 for men's sports the 05-06 year.</p> 
     <p>The Aggie football team plays <a href="/wiki/California_State_University,_Sacramento" title="California State University, Sacramento">Sacramento State</a> in the annual <a href="/wiki/Causeway_Classic" title="Causeway Classic">Causeway Classic</a> for the <a href="/wiki/Causeway_Carriage" title="Causeway Carriage">Causeway Carriage</a>. The team also plays <a href="/wiki/California_Polytechnic_State_University" title="California Polytechnic State University">Cal Poly San Luis Obispo</a> in the annual <a href="/wiki/Battle_for_the_Golden_Horseshoe" title="Battle for the Golden Horseshoe">Battle for the Golden Horseshoe</a>. UC Davis students gather at sporting events to rally as the <a href="/wiki/Aggie_Pack" title="Aggie Pack">Aggie Pack</a>, the largest student-run school spirit organization in the United States. The Aggie Pack cheers on the sports team along with the <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.aggiepack.com/spiritsquad.htm">Spirit Squad</a> to the music of the <a href="/wiki/Cal_Aggie_Marching_Band-uh!" title="Cal Aggie Marching Band-uh!" class="mw-redirect">Cal Aggie Marching Band-uh!</a> and its alumni band. <a href="/wiki/Aggie_Stadium_(UC_Davis)" title="Aggie Stadium (UC Davis)">Aggie Stadium</a> is the home of the UC Davis football and lacrosse teams.</p> 
     <p>UC Davis also had a noteworthy wrestling program, which competed in the Pac-10 at the Division I level. In 2007, UC Davis wrestler Derek Moore gained All-American status, as well as won the NCAA Division I Championships for his weight class. Moore also received the &quot;Most Outstanding Wrestler&quot; award of the NCAA tournament. In doing so, Derek Moore became the first UC Davis student-athlete to become a NCAA champion at the Division I level. That same year, UC Davis finished within the top 25 for Division I collegiate wrestling programs in the country.</p> 
     <p>Wrestling was cut from the athletic department in April 2010. Other cuts included men's swimming, men's indoor track, and women's rowing. The athletic's department had to cut $1.79 million out of the budget. 14 women's teams and 9 men's teams were funded for the 2010-2011 school year.<sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78"><span>[</span>78<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <div class="thumb tleft"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Ucdavis_aggies.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/c/cc/Ucdavis_aggies.png/220px-Ucdavis_aggies.png" width="220" height="229" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/c/cc/Ucdavis_aggies.png/330px-Ucdavis_aggies.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/c/cc/Ucdavis_aggies.png 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Ucdavis_aggies.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf9/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> UC Davis Athletics logo
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>The official school colors are blue and gold. The blue is due to the UC's early connection to Yale<sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79"><span>[</span>79<span>]</span></a></sup> and as a result is often referred to as &quot;<a href="/wiki/Yale_Blue" title="Yale Blue">Yale Blue</a>&quot; (e.g., see),<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80"><span>[</span>80<span>]</span></a></sup> and <sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81"><span>[</span>81<span>]</span></a></sup> although UCD's official blue, usually called &quot;Aggie Blue&quot;, Pantone 295<sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82"><span>[</span>82<span>]</span></a></sup> differs from Yale Blue (approximately Pantone 289)<sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83"><span>[</span>83<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>The official school mascot is the <a href="/wiki/Mustang_(horse)" title="Mustang (horse)" class="mw-redirect">mustang</a>. Students at UC Davis are referred to as Aggies in honor of the school's agricultural heritage. Unlike most colleges, there is a distinction between the name for students and the mascot. There was a movement to change the school's mascot from the mustang to the <a href="/wiki/Dairy_cattle" title="Dairy cattle">cow</a>, but despite student support this was turned down after opposition from alumni. Many people will call the mustang mascot of UC Davis an <a href="/wiki/UC_Davis_Aggies" title="UC Davis Aggies">Aggie</a>, but this is not its proper name; the mustang mascot is named Gunrock. The name dates to 1921 when the US Army brought a thoroughbred horse named <a href="/wiki/Gunrock" title="Gunrock">Gunrock</a> to UC Davis to supply high-quality breeding stock for the <a href="/wiki/US_Cavalry" title="US Cavalry" class="mw-redirect">US Cavalry</a> remount program. The mustang mascot was selected to honor that cavalry horse.</p> 
     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Sustainability">Sustainability</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_California,_Davis&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Sustainability">edit</a>]</span></h2> 
     <p>UC Davis has implemented many environmentally sustainable features on campus. In the Fall of 2010, UCD opened a renovated Dining Commons in the Cuarto living area. The dining hall prides itself on its sustainability and use of local produce. Currently there are two <a href="/wiki/Leadership_in_Energy_and_Environmental_Design" title="Leadership in Energy and Environmental Design">LEED</a>-certified buildings operated by the university ? the Robert Mondavi Institute for Wine and Food Science, which is the first brewery, winery or food-processing facilities in the world to achieve Platinum-level certification, and the Tahoe Center for Environmental Sciences at <a href="/wiki/Lake_Tahoe" title="Lake Tahoe">Lake Tahoe</a>, one of only five laboratories in the world to achieve Platinum-level certification.<sup id="cite_ref-UC_Davis:_Green_Buildings_84-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UC_Davis:_Green_Buildings-84"><span>[</span>84<span>]</span></a></sup> Plans call for additional campus buildings to meet standards equivalent to LEED Silver,<sup id="cite_ref-UC_Davis:_Building_Management_85-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UC_Davis:_Building_Management-85"><span>[</span>85<span>]</span></a></sup> and for the development of UC Davis West Village as a &quot;zero net energy&quot; community.<sup id="cite_ref-UC_Davis:_West_Village_86-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UC_Davis:_West_Village-86"><span>[</span>86<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>The university was given two Best Practice Awards at the 2009 annual Sustainability Conference, held by the University of California, California State University and the California Community Colleges, for the campus's lighting retrofit project and sustainable design in new construction.<sup id="cite_ref-UC_Davis:_Best_Practices_87-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UC_Davis:_Best_Practices-87"><span>[</span>87<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>UC Davis has used the olives from the old trees on campus to produce olive oil<sup id="cite_ref-UC_Davis:_Olive_oil_88-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UC_Davis:_Olive_oil-88"><span>[</span>88<span>]</span></a></sup> and table olives,<sup id="cite_ref-UC_Davis:_Table_Olives_89-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UC_Davis:_Table_Olives-89"><span>[</span>89<span>]</span></a></sup> and the school uses drought-tolerant landscaping on and around campus.<sup id="cite_ref-UC_Davis:_Landscaping_90-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UC_Davis:_Landscaping-90"><span>[</span>90<span>]</span></a></sup> The campus also operates its own landfill, where it converts landfill (methane) gas to energy.<sup id="cite_ref-UC_Davis:_Energy_91-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UC_Davis:_Energy-91"><span>[</span>91<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>For its efforts in campus sustainability, UC Davis earned an A- on the 2010 College Sustainability Report Card, one of 27 schools to achieve the highest grade awarded.<sup id="cite_ref-greenreportcard.org_43-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-greenreportcard.org-43"><span>[</span>43<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>UC Davis became the first University to implement a fee on all single-use bags distributed on campus and is working towards becoming the first university campus to ban plastic bags entirely.<sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92"><span>[</span>92<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>UC Davis is also home to the Agricultural Sustainability Institute (ASI),<sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93"><span>[</span>93<span>]</span></a></sup> which is part of the College of Agricultural and Environmental Sciences (CAES). ASI provides leadership for research, teaching, outreach, and extension efforts in agricultural and food systems sustainability at the Davis campus and throughout the UC system.</p> 
     <p>UC Davis, introduced by Arnold Schwarzenegger as the &quot;environmental capital of the world&quot;,<sup id="cite_ref-GGCS3_94-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GGCS3-94"><span>[</span>94<span>]</span></a></sup> hosted Governors' Global Climate Summit 3 (GGCS3)<sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95"><span>[</span>95<span>]</span></a></sup> which is an international climate forum for the top leaders of local, regional, national and international entities, as well as those from academia, business and nonprofit. The summit featured talks that promised to broaden national partnerships through an increased understanding of unique environmental and economic challenges in the continuation to grow a clean, green economy. The summit included more than 1,500 attendees from more than 80 countries.</p> 
     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="People">People</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_California,_Davis&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: People">edit</a>]</span></h2>

       <li id="cite_note-16"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-16">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://geonames.usgs.gov/pls/gnispublic/f?p=gnispq:3:::NO::P3_FID:2628819">U.S. Geological Survey Geographic Names Information System: University of California, Davis</a></span></li> 
       <li id="cite_note-17"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-17">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">All data are derived from the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Census_Bureau" title="United States Census Bureau">United States Census Bureau</a> reports from the <a href="/wiki/2010_United_States_Census" title="2010 United States Census">2010 United States Census</a>, and are accessible on-line <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://factfinder2.census.gov">here</a>. The data on unmarried partnerships and same-sex married couples are from the Census report DEC_10_SF1_PCT15. All other housing and population data are from Census report DEC_10_DP_DPDP1. Both reports are viewable online or downloadable in a zip file containing a comma-delimited data file. The area data, from which densities are calculated, are available on-line <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.census.gov/geo/www/gazetteer/files/Gaz_places_national.txt">here</a>. Percentage totals may not add to 100% due to rounding. The Census Bureau defines families as a household containing one or more people related to the householder by birth, opposite-sex marriage, or adoption. People living in group quarters are tabulated by the Census Bureau as neither owners nor renters. For further details, see the text files accompanying the data files containing the Census reports mentioned above.</span></li>
